[f]<strong>larumullu</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>lwU;W</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/laru.html#highlulani">laru</a>-<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mullu.html#highlulani">mullu</a>
[e]<em>year-minus_one</em>
[e]<em>lit.:</em> &ldquo;<overline>1</overline>-day&rdquo;
[e]&ldquo;two years ago&rdquo;[/d]
[/d]&date=20180503--------------------------------------------------3
[1]Suffixes
Suffixes can be used to derive new word from existing vocabulary. A suffix beginning with a vowel replaces the final vowel of the base.
[2]Derivational Suffixes
These derive words within a class, <em>i.e.:</em> a noun from a noun, or a verb from a verb.
The augmentative <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/-aku.html#highlulani">-aku</a> <high-lulani>/a&gt;</high-lulani> is most often attached to nouns to reference something large or important. It is rarely used for people.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tissaku.html#highlulani">tissaku</a> <high-lulani>T;s&gt;</high-lulani> <em>wind</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/'isilaku.html#highlulani">&rsquo;isilaku</a> <high-lulani>iSl&gt;</high-lulani> <em>depression</em>[/d]
The diminutive <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/-ini.html#highlulani">-ini</a> <high-lulani>/iN</high-lulani> is used to form words which reference something small or unimportant. When used with animate nouns, it creates a word for the young of non-sapient creatures. However, with sapient creatures, this word is obscene.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/'ahatini.html#highlulani">&rsquo;ahatini</a> <high-lulani>ahTN</high-lulani> <em>contentment</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tissini.html#highlulani">tissini</a> <high-lulani>T;SN</high-lulani> <em>breeze</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qikannini.html#highlulani">qikannini</a> <high-lulani>Qk;NN</high-lulani> <em>puppy</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ranini.html#highlulani">ranini</a> <high-lulani>rNN</high-lulani> <em>potato chips</em>
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/b/bi'ini.html#highlulani">bi&rsquo;ini</a> <high-lulani>BiN</high-lulani> <em>to itch</em>[/d]
The honorific <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/-fi.html#highlulani">-fi</a> <high-lulani>F</high-lulani> confers a nuance of sacredness upon a base word.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/karafi.html#highlulani">karafi</a> <high-lulani>krF</high-lulani> <em>sacredness</em>
[e]<strong>lulanifi</strong> <high-lulani>WlNF</high-lulani> <em>great queen</em>[/d]
The pair <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/-tu'i.html#highlulani">-tu&rsquo;i</a> <high-lulani>ei</high-lulani> and <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/-da.html#highlulani">-da</a> <high-lulani>d</high-lulani> are used to highlight the positive and negative aspects of a word, respectively.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dasatu'i.html#highlulani">dasatu&rsquo;i</a> <high-lulani>dsei</high-lulani> <em>passion</em> / <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dasada.html#highlulani">dasada</a> <high-lulani>dsd</high-lulani> <em>anger</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/ta'itu'i.html#highlulani">ta&rsquo;itu&rsquo;i</a> <high-lulani>tiei</high-lulani> <em>aroma</em> / <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/ta'ida.html#highlulani">ta&rsquo;ida</a> <high-lulani>tid</high-lulani> <em>stink</em>[/d]
[3]Nominal suffixes
These derive nouns from other nouns.
[t]| inanimate base | abstract base
h animate | <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/-rra.html#highlulani">-rra</a><br><high-lulani>;r</high-lulani> | <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/-sa.html#highlulani">-sa</a> / <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/-ri.html#highlulani">-ri</a><br><high-lulani>R . s</high-lulani>
h inanimate |  | <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/-di.html#highlulani">-di</a><br><high-lulani>D</high-lulani>
h abstract | <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/-ja.html#highlulani">-ja</a><br><high-lulani>j</high-lulani> | [/t]
[d mobile-table]
inanimate
[e] &rarr; animate: <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/-rra.html#highlulani">-rra</a> <high-lulani>;r</high-lulani>
[e] &rarr; abstract: <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/-ja.html#highlulani">-ja</a> <high-lulani>j</high-lulani>
abstract
[e] &rarr; animate: <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/-sa.html#highlulani">-sa</a> <high-lulani>s</high-lulani> / <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/-ri.html#highlulani">-ri</a> <high-lulani>R</high-lulani>
[e] &rarr; inanimate: <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/-di.html#highlulani">-di</a> <high-lulani>D</high-lulani>[/d]
The above table shows the suffixes used for deriving nouns between different animacy classes.
An animate noun is derived from an inanimate noun by the suffix  <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/-rra.html#highlulani">-rra</a> <high-lulani>;r</high-lulani>.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tisakarra.html#highlulani">tisakarra</a> <high-lulani>Tsk;r</high-lulani> <em>townsperson</em>[/d]
Both <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/-sa.html#highlulani">-sa</a> <high-lulani>s</high-lulani> and <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/-ri.html#highlulani">-ri</a> <high-lulani>R</high-lulani> derive an animate noun from an abstract noun, however, these are not predictable. For instance, note the difference between <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dis.sa.html#highlulani">dis&middot;sa</a> <high-lulani>D;zs</high-lulani> <em>youth</em> and <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dissuri.html#highlulani">dissuri</a> <high-lulani>D;zR</high-lulani> <em>stranger</em>. Other examples are:
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pucasa.html#highlulani">pucasa</a> <high-lulani>ocs</high-lulani> <em>optimist</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sasa.html#highlulani">sasa</a> <high-lulani>ss</high-lulani> <em>introvert</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dattusa.html#highlulani">dattusa</a> <high-lulani>d;es</high-lulani> <em>god</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mulisa.html#highlulani">mulisa</a> <high-lulani>ULs</high-lulani> <em>fool</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/luxirasa.html#highlulani">luxirasa</a> <high-lulani>WXrs</high-lulani> <em>twin</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tuhhisa.html#highlulani">tuhhisa</a> <high-lulani>e;Hs</high-lulani> <em>farmer</em>
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/'axasiri.html#highlulani">&rsquo;axasiri</a> <high-lulani>axSR</high-lulani> <em>adult</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/'asilari.html#highlulani">&rsquo;asilari</a> <high-lulani>aSlR</high-lulani> <em>friend</em>[/d]
The <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/-ri.html#highlulani">-ri</a> <high-lulani>R</high-lulani> suffix also denotes people from a particular place.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tinalliri.html#highlulani">Tinalliri</a> <high-lulani>Tn;LR</high-lulani> <em>Tinellbian</em>[/d]
The suffix <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/-di.html#highlulani">-di</a> <high-lulani>D</high-lulani> derives an inanimate noun from something abstract, and <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/-ja.html#highlulani">-ja</a> <high-lulani>j</high-lulani> does the opposite.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sinnadi.html#highlulani">sinnadi</a> <high-lulani>S;nD</high-lulani> <em>book</em>
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ru'ihaja.html#highlulani">ru&rsquo;ihaja</a> <high-lulani>wihj</high-lulani> <em>history</em>[/d]
The suffix <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/-li.html#highlulani">-li</a> <high-lulani>L</high-lulani> derives nouns which are somehow distinct from their stem.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/daruli.html#highlulani">daruli</a> <high-lulani>dwL</high-lulani> <em>wrong way</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/g/gusuli.html#highlulani">gusuli</a> <em>non-Guozu person</em>[/d]
The names of parts of the body are derived using <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/-kku.html#highlulani">-kku</a> <high-lulani>;&gt;</high-lulani> on either nouns or verbs.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/'itikku.html#highlulani">&rsquo;itikku</a> <high-lulani>iT;&gt;</high-lulani> <em>breast</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mulukku.html#highlulani">mulukku</a> <high-lulani>UW;&gt;</high-lulani> <em>heart</em>
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dasikku.html#highlulani">dasikku</a> <high-lulani>dS;&gt;</high-lulani> <em>digestive system</em>[/d]
The animate giver of the inanimate or abstract base is denoted by <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/-mi.html#highlulani">-mi</a> <high-lulani>M</high-lulani>.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/'aggami.html#highlulani">&rsquo;aggami</a> <high-lulani>a;gM</high-lulani> <em>police officer</em> / <em>law giver</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sa'imi.html#highlulani">Sa&rsquo;imi</a> <high-lulani>siM</high-lulani> <em>Caemi</em> / <em>light giver</em>[/d]
The feminine and masculine are denoted by <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/-qi.html#highlulani">-qi</a> and <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/-kati.html#highlulani">-kati</a> respectively, however, they are infrequently used.
[3]Verbal suffixes
These are only applied to verbs.
The suffix <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/-ni.html#highlulani">-ni</a> <high-lulani>N</high-lulani> is used to derive inceptive verbs.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/ducini.html#highlulani">ducini</a> <high-lulani>ECN</high-lulani> <em>to receive</em>[/d]
The suffix <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/-ulu.html#highlulani">-ulu</a> <high-lulani>/uW</high-lulani> denotes reversal of an action, and can only be applied to stem verbs.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lulu.html#highlulani">lulu</a> <high-lulani>WW</high-lulani> <em>to undo</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/jannulu.html#highlulani">jannulu</a> <high-lulani>j;IW</high-lulani> <em>to return</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/turulu.html#highlulani">turulu</a> <high-lulani>ewW</high-lulani> <em>to open</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/ju'ulu.html#highlulani">ju&rsquo;ulu</a> <high-lulani>YuW</high-lulani> <em>to unlink</em>[/d]
The repetition marker <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/-tuni.html#highlulani">-tuni</a> <high-lulani>eN</high-lulani> has similar form and meaning to the full verb <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tuni.html#highlulani">tuni</a> <high-lulani>eN</high-lulani> <em>repeat</em>.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/latuni.html#highlulani">latuni</a> <high-lulani>leN</high-lulani> <em>to do again</em>[/d]
The augmentative <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/-ssasu.html#highlulani">-ssasu</a> <high-lulani>;sz</high-lulani> is used specifically for verbs.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/b/bi'u.html#highlulani">bi&rsquo;u</a>ssasu <high-lulani>Bu;sz</high-lulani> <em>to really hurt</em>[/d]
[3]Auxiliary Infix
The infix <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/-ar-.html#highlulani">-ar-</a> is placed before the final vowel of auxiliaries, and denotes an end to the action described by the sentence.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lanaru.html#highlulani">lanaru</a> <high-lulani>lnw</high-lulani> <em>will finish doing</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/nagari.html#highlulani">nagari</a> <high-lulani>ngR</high-lulani> <em>will finish being</em>[/d]
[3]Adverbial Suffixes
There are two kinds of negation for adverbs. The suffix <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/h/-hita.html#highlulani">-hita</a> <high-lulani>Ht</high-lulani> is standard negation.
[d wordlist]
[f]<strong>jamihita</strong> <high-lulani>jMHt</high-lulani> <em>not in evidence</em>
[e]<strong>&rsquo;ilihita</strong> <high-lulani>iLHt</high-lulani> <em>not in reality</em>[/d]
On the other hand, <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/-ma.html#highlulani">-ma</a> <high-lulani>m</high-lulani> forms terminatives, <em>i.e.</em>: the situation described by the adverb was true in the past, but no longer applies.
[d wordlist]
[f]<strong>nufirama</strong> <em>no longer wanting</em>
[e]<strong>dumima</strong> <em>no longer trying</em>[/d]
[2]Nominalisation
These derive a noun from another part of speech, most often a verb.
The suffix <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/-qa.html#highlulani">-qa</a> <high-lulani>q</high-lulani> derives generic nouns from numerals or alienable genitive pronouns.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/disiqa.html#highlulani">disiqa</a> <high-lulani>DSq</high-lulani> <em>hers</em>
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/nuruqa.html#highlulani">nuruqa</a> <high-lulani>Iwq</high-lulani> <em>the four of them</em>
[/d]
The suffix <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/-muka.html#highlulani">-muka</a> <high-lulani>Uk</high-lulani> is used with prepositional phrases.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/disinnamuka.html#highlulani">disinnamuka</a> <high-lulani>DS;nUk</high-lulani> <em>prologue</em>
[/d]
Other suffixes in this group are divided into animacy classes.
[3]Abstract
The productive general suffix <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/-'a.html#highlulani">-&rsquo;a</a> <high-lulani>a</high-lulani> derives abstract nouns.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/c/cura'a.html#highlulani">cura&rsquo;a</a> <high-lulani>yra</high-lulani> <em>time</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qacca'a.html#highlulani">qacca&rsquo;a</a> <high-lulani>q;ca</high-lulani> <em>choice</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pa'a.html#highlulani">pa&rsquo;a</a> <high-lulani>pa</high-lulani> <em>thought</em>[/d]
The suffix <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/-ru.html#highlulani">-ru</a> <high-lulani>w</high-lulani> forms gerunds.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dasi.html#highlulani">dasi</a>ru <high-lulani>dSw</high-lulani> <em>eating</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/janni.html#highlulani">janni</a>ru <high-lulani>j;Nw</high-lulani> <em>moving</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/h/huba.html#highlulani">huba</a>ru <high-lulani>Vbw</high-lulani> <em>breathing</em>[/d]
Application of <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/-ppa.html#highlulani">-ppa</a> <high-lulani>;p</high-lulani> derives terms for times and occasions.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dasippa.html#highlulani">dasippa</a> <high-lulani>dS;p</high-lulani> <em>mealtime</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sikuppa.html#highlulani">sikuppa</a> <high-lulani>S&gt;;p</high-lulani> <em>funeral</em>[/d]
The suffix <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/-ahi.html#highlulani">-ahi</a> is used with adverbs.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/nufirahi.html#highlulani">nufirahi</a> <high-lulani>IFrH</high-lulani> <em>expectation</em>[/d]
[3]Inanimate
The patientive suffix <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/-du.html#highlulani">-du</a> <high-lulani>E</high-lulani> is applied to stem verbs.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dasidu.html#highlulani">dasidu</a> <high-lulani>dSE</high-lulani> <em>food</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/maladu.html#highlulani">maladu</a> <high-lulani>mlE</high-lulani> <em>reflection</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kassudu.html#highlulani">kassudu</a> <high-lulani>k;zE</high-lulani>  <em>trade goods</em>[/d]
The instrumental suffix <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/-ffi.html#highlulani">-ffi</a> <high-lulani>;F</high-lulani> is applied to a verb.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dasiffi.html#highlulani">dasiffi</a> <high-lulani>dS;F</high-lulani> <em>cutlery, tools for eating</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sikuffi.html#highlulani">sikuffi</a> <high-lulani>S&gt;;F</high-lulani> <em>spear, tool for killing</em>[/d]
The suffix <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/-kku.html#highlulani">-kku</a> <high-lulani>;&gt;</high-lulani> derives names for parts of the body from verbs or nouns.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dasikku.html#highlulani">dasikku</a> <high-lulani>dS;&gt;</high-lulani> <em>digestive system</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/'itikku.html#highlulani">&rsquo;itikku</a> <high-lulani>iT;&gt;</high-lulani> <em>breast</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mulukku.html#highlulani">mulukku</a> <high-lulani>UW;&gt;</high-lulani> <em>heart</em>[/d]
When applied to a number, <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/-ssiji.html#highlulani">-ssiji</a> <high-lulani>;SJ</high-lulani> gives rise to the names of shapes.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kifissiji.html#highlulani">kifissiji</a> <high-lulani>KF;SJ</high-lulani> <em>triangle</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/nurussiji.html#highlulani">nurussiji</a> <high-lulani>Iw;SJ</high-lulani> <em>quadrilateral</em>[/d]
[3]Animate
There are three suffixes for deriving animate nouns from verbs. The suffix <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/-la'i.html#highlulani">-la&rsquo;i</a> is used with intransitive verbs, while <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/b/-ba.html#highlulani">-ba</a> and <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/-pu'a.html#highlulani">-pu&rsquo;a</a> derive generic agents and patients respectively.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/narala'i.html#highlulani">narala&rsquo;i</a> <high-lulani>nrli</high-lulani> <em>sleeper</em>
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/'ussaba.html#highlulani">&rsquo;ussaba</a> <high-lulani>u;sb</high-lulani> <em>follower</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/c/caba.html#highlulani">caba</a> <high-lulani>cb</high-lulani> <em>helper</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/h/hisuba.html#highlulani">hisuba</a> <high-lulani>Hzb</high-lulani> <em>administrator</em>
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/ju'ipu'a.html#highlulani">ju&rsquo;ipu&rsquo;a</a> <high-lulani>Yioa</high-lulani> <em>group</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lu'ipu'a.html#highlulani">lu&rsquo;ipu&rsquo;a</a> <high-lulani>Wioa</high-lulani> <em>lover</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/c/cikkipu'a.html#highlulani">cikkipu&rsquo;a</a> <high-lulani>C;Koa</high-lulani> <em>telepath</em>[/d]
[2]Adverbialisation
The pair of suffixes <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/-atinna.html#highlulani">-atinna</a> <high-lulani>/aT;n</high-lulani> and <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/-niqqi.html#highlulani">-niqqi</a> <high-lulani>N;Q</high-lulani> derive adverbs from verbs and nouns respectively.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/'usatinna.html#highlulani">&rsquo;usatinna</a> <high-lulani>usT;n</high-lulani> <em>visibly</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/katinna.html#highlulani">katinna</a> <high-lulani>kT;n</high-lulani> <em>increasingly</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lu'atinna.html#highlulani">lu&rsquo;atinna</a> <high-lulani>WaT;n</high-lulani> <em>lovingly</em>
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/'ahatiniqqi.html#highlulani">&rsquo;ahatiniqqi</a> <high-lulani>ahTN;Q</high-lulani> <em>happily</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/'isilakuniqqi.html#highlulani">&rsquo;isilakuniqqi</a> <high-lulani>iSl&gt;N;Q</high-lulani> <em>depressingly</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/b/bataniqqi.html#highlulani">bataniqqi</a> <high-lulani>btN;Q</high-lulani> <em>carefully</em>

[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/g/ga'iniqqi.html#highlulani">ga&rsquo;iniqqi</a> <high-lulani>giN;Q</high-lulani> <em>in time</em>[/d]
&date=20180503--------------------------------------------------4
[1]Determiners
A determiner can be used to narrow the reference of a noun. They appear at the end of a noun phrase, after any normal suffixes. They do not move the stress of the noun, and can only receive up to secondary stress themselves.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/c/cama.html#highlulani">cama</a> <high-lulani>cm</high-lulani> <em>usual</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/nisa.html#highlulani">nisa</a> <high-lulani>Ns</high-lulani> <em>only</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sabufi.html#highlulani">sabufi</a> <high-lulani>sOF</high-lulani> <em>different</em>[/d]
[3]Quantity
These are used to answer &rdquo;how many?&rdquo;
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mimu'i.html#highlulani">mimu&rsquo;i</a> <high-lulani>MUi</high-lulani> <em>some</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lumi.html#highlulani">lumi</a> <high-lulani>WM</high-lulani> <em>several</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/raqi.html#highlulani">raqi</a> <high-lulani>rQ</high-lulani> <em>more</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/'uhu.html#highlulani">&rsquo;uhu</a> <high-lulani>uV</high-lulani> <em>many</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/takki.html#highlulani">takki</a> <high-lulani>t;K</high-lulani> <em>many</em>[/d]
[3]Choice
There are two sets of determiners that are both used to select a part from the whole. One group is used with count nouns, the other with mass nouns.
[4]Count Nouns
These refer to particular members of a group.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/c/ca.html#highlulani">ca</a> <high-lulani>c</high-lulani> <em>only</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/fi'atu.html#highlulani">fi&rsquo;atu</a> <high-lulani>Fae</high-lulani> <em>certain</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tapa.html#highlulani">tapa</a> <high-lulani>tp</high-lulani> <em>next</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/c/cari.html#highlulani">cari</a> <high-lulani>cR</high-lulani> <em>remaining</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qafa.html#highlulani">qafa</a> <high-lulani>qf</high-lulani> <em>last</em>[/d]
[4]Mass Nouns
These refer to sections of a substance.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/c/cari.html#highlulani">cari</a> <high-lulani>cR</high-lulani> <em>remaining</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sukki.html#highlulani">sukki</a> <high-lulani>z;K</high-lulani> <em>entire</em>[/d]
[3]Degree
These mark the degree to which the noun matches its referent.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/nata.html#highlulani">nata</a> <high-lulani>nt</high-lulani> <em>complete</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/naci.html#highlulani">naci</a> <high-lulani>nC</high-lulani> <em>somewhat</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/ji'a.html#highlulani">ji&rsquo;a</a> <high-lulani>Ja</high-lulani> <em>not</em>[/d]&date=20180503--------------------------------------------------3
[1]Deixis
Deixis encompasses words and phrases which rely on an external context to complete their meaning.
[2]Topicality
Once a topic is introduced in a discourse or narrative, it can be assumed to be the subject until changed.
[2]Pro-forms
The two groups of pro-forms are classified on the basis of their semantic properties.
<a href="definitepro-forms.html">Definite pro-forms</a> are those that encode case, person, animacy and topicality.  <a href="indefinitepro-forms.html">Indefinite pro-forms</a> comprise the remaining deictic terms.
&date=20180505--------------------------------------------------4
[1]Personal Pronouns
These are a closed class. They are marked for <a href="../../syntax/case.html">case</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grammatical_person">person</a>. The third person pronouns are additionally marked for topicality or <a href="../nouns.html#animacy">animacy</a>. The alienable genitive acts as the nominal head of a possessive phrase, the inalienable genitive is a determiner, and the other pronouns all act as nouns.

[2]Number
Pronouns are not generally marked for number.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>&#x294;usu ra&rsquo;u pannaxa. / &#x294;usu ra&rsquo;u pannaxa&rsquo;uxxi.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.uz / ru / p;nxu;X . uz / ru / p;nx.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/'usu.html#highlulani">&#x294;usu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra'u.html#highlulani">ra&rsquo;u</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pannaxa.html#highlulani">pannaxa</a>. / <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/'usu.html#highlulani">&#x294;usu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra'u.html#highlulani">ra&rsquo;u</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pannaxa'uxxi.html#highlulani">pannaxa&rsquo;uxxi</a>.
[e]<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>1int</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">first person intransitive</span></span> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>prs;sta</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">present stative</span></span> <em>warrior</em>. / <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>1int</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">first person intransitive</span></span> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>prs;sta</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">present stative</span></span> <em>army</em>.
[e]&ldquo;I am a warrior.&rdquo; / &ldquo;We are an army.&rdquo;[/d]
However, if reference is made to a group that includes more than one of these persons, then additional pronouns can be constructed. The second person transitive pronoun <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/-fu.html#highlulani">-fu</a> <high-lulani>v</high-lulani> <em>and you</em> can be suffixed to the first person pronouns to form first person inclusive plural pronouns. The third person intransitive inanimate pronoun <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/-pa.html#highlulani">-pa</a> <high-lulani>p</high-lulani> <em>and them </em>can be suffixed to first or second person pronouns, including those with -fu, to form other plural pronouns. These pronouns have no inalienable genitive form.

[e]&ldquo;You and he have betrayed me!&rdquo;[/d]
[2]Genitive Forms
The genitive forms mark a connection between nouns, including one noun possessing another.
[3]Alienable Possession
Possession is alienable when the possessed item can be transferred from one owner to another. Alienable possessions include objects bought or received by a person. There is no inanimate alienable genitive pronoun as objects cannot own anything.
The structure of the possessive phrase for alienable possession is &ldquo;<em>possessor</em> <strong>genitive</strong> <em>possessed&rdquo;.</em>

[3]Inalienable Possession
Inalienable possession refers to items which are unable to be transferred from one individual to another. Inalienable possessions include relatives, parts of the body and objects created by a person.
For inalienable possession, as well as genitive constructions that do not involve literal possession, the structure is &ldquo;<em>possessed</em>-<strong>genitive</strong> <em>possessor</em>&ldquo;, that is, the genitive marker is an enclitic on the possessed item. This marker is always the third person inanimate genitive pronoun, unless the possessor is a plain pronoun.

Proximate forms have referents physically or psychologically near the speaker, whereas distal forms are used when the referent is far away. Interrogative forms are used in questions, and negative forms are used in negative sentences. Universal means &ldquo;all&rdquo; or &ldquo;every&rdquo;, and existential means &ldquo;some&rdquo; or &ldquo;any&rdquo;.
The existential markers are also used in complements.

[e]<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>1int</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">first person intransitive</span></span> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>com</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">complementiser</span></span> <em>name</em> <em>something</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>prs;gno</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">present gnomic</span></span> <em>learn.</em>
[e]&ldquo;I learned what her name is.&rdquo;[/d]
[2]Object Noun
Object nouns are pronouns. Unlike some personal pronouns, these are not marked for animacy, and are thus used to represent people, animals or things.
[d folding]

Manner pro-forms are used to refer to the way in which an action is undertaken. They function as modal adverbs in active sentences, <em>i.e.:</em> sentences with overt or implied auxiliaries of <a href="../auxiliaries.html#activityversusstate">activity</a>.

[1]Conjunctions
Conjunctions are a closed class of words which are used to join phrases or clauses together.
[2]Phrase-level Conjunctions
These conjunctions are used to join words or phrases. They are enclitics on the second and subsequent nouns.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/-ta.html#highlulani">-ta</a> <high-lulani>t</high-lulani> <em>and</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/-sija.html#highlulani">-sija</a> <high-lulani>Sj</high-lulani> <em>or</em>[/d]
[2]Clause-level Conjunctions
These conjunctions are used to join clauses or sentences. They are used as independent words.
[3]Coordinating Conjunctions
Coordinating conjunctions are used to separate two matrix clauses. They are placed at the beginning of the second clause.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qu.html#highlulani">qu</a> <high-lulani>A</high-lulani> <em>and</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/nuki.html#highlulani">nuki</a> <high-lulani>IK</high-lulani> <em>or</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pada.html#highlulani">pada</a> <high-lulani>pd</high-lulani> <em>and then</em>[/d]
[3]Subordinating Conjunctions
Subordinating conjunctions are used to introduce a dependent clause. See the section on <a href="../syntax/dependentclauses.html#subordinateclauses">subordinate clauses</a> for syntactical information.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/surra.html#highlulani">surra</a> <em>if</em>

[1]Particles
There are very few particles. These are simply words that do not fit neatly into any other category. This includes:
[l]<a href="interjections.html">interjections</a>,
<a href="../../apocrypha/numbers.html">numbers</a>,
pronouns of the <a href="../deixis/personalpronouns.html#alienablepossession">alienable genitive</a>,
<a href="../../syntax/dependentclauses.html#contentclauses">content</a> and <a href="../../syntax/dependentclauses.html#relativeclauses">relative</a> clause introductory markers, and
the <a href="../../syntax/comparatives.html#superlative">superlative</a> marker.[/l]&date=20180503--------------------------------------------------4
[1]Interjections
These are exclamations that do not fit the syntactic rules of the other parts of speech, hence their classification among the particles. All interjections end with the same vowel, either naturally,
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/ta.html#highlulani">ta</a> <high-lulani>t</high-lulani> <em>um</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/ti'a.html#highlulani">ti&rsquo;a</a> <high-lulani>Ta</high-lulani>  <em>oh!</em>[/d]
or because the interjection marker <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/-a.html#highlulani">-a</a> <high-lulani>/a</high-lulani> has derived them from nouns or verbs.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mica.html#highlulani">mica</a> <high-lulani>Mc</high-lulani> <em>hello</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/nara.html#highlulani">nara</a> <high-lulani>nr</high-lulani> <em>goodbye; good night</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/h/hacca.html#highlulani">hacca</a> <high-lulani>h;c</high-lulani> <em>good morning</em>

[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/h/hira.html#highlulani">hira</a> <high-lulani>Hr</high-lulani> <em>please; thank-you</em>[/d]
&date=20180503--------------------------------------------------2
[1]Syntax
High Lulani is head-initial in compounds, but tends to be head-final in phrases and clauses. The language has Subject-Verb-Object order, but shows signs of an SOV nature, as dative and ablative complements become more common.
&date=20180223--------------------------------------------------3
[1]Case
[2]Alignment
The three basic arguments for any verb (intransitive subjects, transitive subjects and transitive objects) are marked in High Lulani. Because intransitive subjects cannot co-occur with transitive arguments, it is possible to mark either of the transitive arguments in the same way as the intransitive without confusion. In the ergative alignment, it is the transitive object that is marked the same as the intransitive subject. In accusative alignment, it is instead the transitive subject that shares marking with intransitive subjects. In either alignment, the intransitive case is the one treated like the intransitive subject, and the transitive case is the other.
High Lulani has an ergativity split, made down aspectual lines. A clause using dynamic or iterative auxiliaries uses ergative alignment; gnomic, stative and negative aspects attract the accusative.
[2]Core Cases
The core cases mark the basic arguments of the verb. Common or proper nouns have no case markings for these, but the pronouns have different forms. Therefore only pronouns show the alignment of a sentence.
[3]Intransitive
The intransitive case is used for the sole argument of an intransitive verb and for the unmarked argument of transitive sentences. This case is also used for adpositions.
[3]Transitive
The transitive case is used for the marked argument of transitive sentences, that is, the object in an accusative clause, and the subject in ergative clauses.
[2]Oblique Cases
The two oblique cases are marked on the pronouns. For common and proper nouns, a clitic with the same form as the appropriate third person inanimate pronoun is placed before the noun phrase.
Sometimes the verb requires an oblique rather than a traditional object. In these cases, the subject is usually in intransitive case, although it is not incorrect to use transitive case with dynamic and iterative auxiliaries.
[3]Ablative
The ablative case is used to mark the proximate cause or the instigator of an action. With verbs of transfer or motion, it is also used to mark the source of a movement.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sacu.html#highlulani">sacu</a> <high-lulani>sy</high-lulani> <em>because of you</em> / <em>from you</em>[/d]
The clitic is <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kalu-.html#highlulani">kalu-</a> <high-lulani>kW</high-lulani>.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>kaluTinalli janni</strong>
[e]<high-lulani> kWTn;L / j;N</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kalu-.html#highlulani">kalu-</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tinalli.html#highlulani">Tinalli</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/janni.html#highlulani">janni</a>
[e]<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>abl</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">ablative</span></span>-<em>Tinellb move</em>

[3]Dative
The dative case was originally only used to mark the receiver with verbs of giving and transfer. The meaning has since broadened to show indirectness on the part of the patient for a number of verbs, including verbs of perception and emotion.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pixi.html#highlulani">pixi</a> <high-lulani>PX</high-lulani> <em>to me</em>
[d folding]
[f]<strong>ku&#x294;irri&rsquo;a janni</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>&gt;;i;Ra / j;N</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/ku-.html#highlulani">ku-</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/'irri'a.html#highlulani">&#x294;irri&rsquo;a</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/janni.html#highlulani">janni</a>

[e]&ldquo;go to Ir&igrave;a&rdquo;[/d]
[/d]
The clitic is <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/ku-.html#highlulani">ku-</a> <high-lulani>&gt;</high-lulani> .
[d folding]
[f]<strong>kululani kuffa</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>&gt;WlN / &gt;;f</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/ku-.html#highlulani">ku-</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lulani.html#highlulani">lulani</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kuffa.html#highlulani">kuffa</a>
[e]<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>dat</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">dative</span></span>-<em>queen give</em>
[e]&ldquo;give to the queen&rdquo;[/d]&date=20180503--------------------------------------------------3
[1]Matrix Clauses
The standard word order for matrix clauses is:
Subject &dash; Auxiliary &dash; Adposition - Oblique &dash; Verb &dash; Object &dash; Adverb.
None of these slots are compulsorily filled. If a subject is obvious from context, or is the same as that of the immediately prior sentence, it can be dropped. The adverb can act as a pro-sentence.
[2]Intransitive Clauses
As already discussed, intransitive clauses do not have objects.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Mihu ra&rsquo;u nara.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.MV / ru / nr.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mihu.html#highlulani">Mihu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra'u.html#highlulani">ra&rsquo;u</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/nara.html#highlulani">nara</a>.
[e]<small-caps>3int</small-caps> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>prs;sta</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">present stative</span></span> <em>sleep</em>
[e]&ldquo;He is asleep.&rdquo;[/d]
[2]Transitive Clauses
Transitive clauses do require an object.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>&#x294;usu ru lu&rsquo;i fu.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.uz / w / Wi / v.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/'usu.html#highlulani">&#x294;usu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ru.html#highlulani">ru</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lu'i.html#highlulani">lu&rsquo;i</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/fu.html#highlulani">fu</a>.
[e]<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>1int</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">first person intransitive</span></span> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>prs;gno</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">present gnomic</span></span> <em>love</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>2tra</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">second person transitive</span></span>.
[e]&ldquo;I love you.&rdquo;[/d]
Sometimes the object is in an oblique case.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Mihu ra&rsquo;u kuqikanni &rsquo;usa.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.MV / ru / &gt;Qk;N / us.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mihu.html#highlulani">Mihu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra'u.html#highlulani">ra&rsquo;u</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/ku.html#highlulani">ku</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qikanni.html#highlulani">qikanni</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/'usa.html#highlulani">&rsquo;usa</a>.
[e]<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>3ani;int</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">animate third person intransitive</span></span> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>prs;sta</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">present stative</span></span> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>dat</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">dative</span></span><em>-dog see</em>.
[e]&ldquo;She can see the dog.&rdquo;[/d]
[2]Copular Sentences
Copular sentences do not have a main verb. These sentences are used to show an equivalence relationship between two nouns, or to show that one noun is an element of the set described by the other noun. They are transitive sentences.
[d folding]
[e]<strong>Mihu lanu julliga.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.MV / lI / Y;Lg.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mihu.html#highlulani">Mihu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lanu.html#highlulani">lanu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/julliga.html#highlulani">julliga</a>.
[e]<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>3ani;int</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">animate third person intransitive</span></span> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>fut;dyn</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">future dynamic</span></span> <em>married_woman</em>
[e]&ldquo;She will become a married woman.&rdquo;[/d]
Another use of copular sentences is to tell the location of something in relation to something else.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Pa ra&rsquo;u di&rsquo;i&rsquo;uja.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.p / ru / Diuj.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pa.html#highlulani">Pa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra'u.html#highlulani">ra&rsquo;u</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/di.html#highlulani">di</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/'i'uja.html#highlulani">&rsquo;i&rsquo;uja</a>.
[e]<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>3ina;int</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">inanimate third person intransitive</span></span> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>prs;gno</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">present gnomic</span></span> <em>down-table</em>
[e]&ldquo;It&rsquo;s under the table.&rdquo;[/d]
The copular sentence structure for ownership is as follows. It has the possessor in the dative case, and the possessum as the subject.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Sunu ru pixi.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.zI / w / PX.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sunu.html#highlulani">Sunu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ru.html#highlulani">ru</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pixi.html#highlulani">pixi</a>.
[e]<em>Cloak</em> <small-caps>prs;gno 1dat</small-caps>
[e]I have a cloak.[/d]
The arguments may be swapped without a change in meaning.
[d folding]
[e]<strong>Pixi ru sunu.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.PX / w / zI.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pixi.html#highlulani">Pixi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ru.html#highlulani">ru</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sunu.html#highlulani">sunu</a>.
[e]<small-caps>1dat prs;gno</small-caps><em> cloak.</em>
[e]I have a cloak.[/d]
[2]Contrasting Pronouns
These example sentences have been given to clarify alignment and the correct use of pronouns with different auxiliaries.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Mihu qixa miku.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.MV / Qx / M&gt;.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mihu.html#highlulani">Mihu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qixa.html#highlulani">qixa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/miku.html#highlulani">miku</a>.
[e]<small-caps>3ani.int pst;dyn</small-caps> <em>red</em>
[e]&ldquo;She turned red.&rdquo;[/d]
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Mihu pi miku.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.MV / P / M&gt;.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mihu.html#highlulani">Mihu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pi.html#highlulani">pi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/miku.html#highlulani">miku</a>.
[e]<small-caps>3ani.int pst;sta</small-caps> <em>red</em>
[e]&ldquo;She was red.&rdquo;[/d]
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Quhu qixa dasi pa.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.AV / Qx / dS / p.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/quhu.html#highlulani">Quhu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qixa.html#highlulani">qixa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dasi.html#highlulani">dasi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pa.html#highlulani">pa</a>.
[e]<small-caps>3ani.tra pst;dyn</small-caps> <em>eat</em><small-caps> 3ina.int</small-caps>
[e]&ldquo;She ate it.&rdquo;[/d]
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Mihu pi dasi &rsquo;iffa.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.MV / P / dS / i;f.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mihu.html#highlulani">Mihu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pi.html#highlulani">pi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dasi.html#highlulani">dasi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/'iffa.html#highlulani">&rsquo;iffa</a>.
[e]<small-caps>3ani.int pst;sta</small-caps> <em>eat</em><small-caps> 3ina.tra</small-caps>
[e]&ldquo;She was eating it.&rdquo;[/d]
As can be seen, the only time the transitive case is used for the subject of a clause is in transitive (as well as copular) sentences using dynamic or iterative auxiliaries.
&date=20180503--------------------------------------------------3
[1]Argument Promotion
The first noun in a clause is the subject, which is prototypically the agent in transitive sentences and the patient in intransitive sentences. However, suffixes can be added to the verb to promote other nouns in the clause, other than the genitive.
There are three such verbal suffixes, which can be stacked, however, once something has been shifted from the subject position, it can&rsquo;t be promoted again.
[2]Passive
The passive suffix promotes the object. This suffix has the forms:
[l] <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/-'illu.html#highlulani">-&rsquo;illu</a> <high-lulani>i;W</high-lulani> when the last element of a verb is monosyllabic,
<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/-ilu.html#highlulani">-ilu</a> <high-lulani>/iW</high-lulani> replacing the final vowel if the final consonant is geminated, and
<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/-illu.html#highlulani">-illu</a> <high-lulani>/i;W</high-lulani> replacing the final vowel of the verb elsewise.[/l]
The old subject is then marked with the ablative case. A sentence with this marker is intransitive. The demoted item is not compulsory, but if it is put in, it is the first ablative-marked noun in the new sentence.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Fu qixa kissa kilatu&rsquo;i!</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.v / Qx / K;s / Klei.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/fu.html#highlulani">Fu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qixa.html#highlulani">qixa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kissa.html#highlulani">kissa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kilatu'i.html#highlulani">kilatu&rsquo;i</a>!
[e]<small-caps>2tra pst;dyn</small-caps> <em>fight deer</em>
[e]&ldquo;You fought a deer!&rdquo;[/d]
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Kilatu&rsquo;i qixa (sacu) kissilu.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.Klei / Qx / sy / K;SW.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kilatu'i.html#highlulani">Kilatu&rsquo;i</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qixa.html#highlulani">qixa</a> (<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sacu.html#highlulani">sacu</a>) <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kissa.html#highlulani">kissa</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/-ilu.html#highlulani">-ilu</a>.
[e]<em>deer</em> <small-caps>pst;dyn (2abl)</small-caps> <em>fight</em><small-caps>-psv</small-caps>
[e]&ldquo;A deer was fought (by you).&rdquo;[/d]
[2]Ablative
The ablative suffix promotes the ablative. It has the form:
[l] <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/-ka.html#highlulani">-ka</a> <high-lulani>k</high-lulani> when the final consonant of a verb is geminate, or
<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/-kka.html#highlulani">-kka</a> <high-lulani>;k</high-lulani> elsewise.[/l]
The old subject is demoted to object, and the old object is demoted to dative. A sentence with this marker is transitive. The first dative-marked noun in the new sentence is the demoted item.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Lulani qixa kalukimilli dasi qasa.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.WlN / Qx / kWKM;L / dS / qs.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lulani.html#highlulani">Lulani</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qixa.html#highlulani">qixa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kalu-.html#highlulani">kalu-</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kimilli.html#highlulani">kimilli</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dasi.html#highlulani">dasi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qasa.html#highlulani">qasa</a>.
[e]<em>queen pst;dyn abl-king</em> <em>eat</em> <em>fish</em>
[e]&ldquo;The queen ate a fish because of the king.&rdquo;[/d]
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Kimilli qixa kuqasa dasikka lulani.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.KM;L / Qx / &gt;qs / dS;k / WlN.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kimilli.html#highlulani">Kimilli</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qixa.html#highlulani">qixa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/ku-.html#highlulani">ku-</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qasa.html#highlulani">qasa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dasi.html#highlulani">dasi</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/-kka.html#highlulani">-kka</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lulani.html#highlulani">lulani</a>.
[e]<em>king pst;dyn dat-fish</em> <em>eat</em><small-caps>-abp</small-caps> <em>queen</em><small-caps>.</small-caps>
[e]&ldquo;The king made the queen eat fish.&rdquo;[/d]
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Kimilli qixa (kal&middot;lani) dasilluka qasa.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.KM;L / Qx / kWWlN / dS;Wk / qs.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kimilli.html#highlulani">Kimilli</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qixa.html#highlulani">qixa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kalu-.html#highlulani">kalu-</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lulani.html#highlulani">lulani</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dasi.html#highlulani">dasi</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/-illu.html#highlulani">-illu</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/-ka.html#highlulani">-ka</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qasa.html#highlulani">qasa</a>.
[e]<em>king</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>pst;dyn</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">past dynamic</span></span> (<small-caps>abl-queen)</small-caps> <em>eat</em><small-caps>-psv-abp</small-caps> <em>fish</em>
[e]&ldquo;The king made the fish get eaten (by the queen).&rdquo;[/d]
[2]Dative
The suffix <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/x/-xa.html#highlulani">-xa</a> promotes a dative. The old subject is demoted to object, and the old object (if any) is demoted to dative. A sentence with this marker is transitive.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Mulisa ru kuquxi kuffa laqqu.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.ULs / w / &gt;AX / &gt;;f / l;A.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mulisa.html#highlulani">Mulisa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ru.html#highlulani">ru</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/ku-.html#highlulani">ku-</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/quxi.html#highlulani">quxi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kuffa.html#highlulani">kuffa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/laqqu.html#highlulani">laqqu</a>.
[e]<em>fool</em> <small-caps>prs;gno dat</small-caps>-<em>mountain give money</em>.
[e]&ldquo;A fool gives money to the mountain.&rdquo;[/d]
[d folding]
[e]<strong>Quxi ru kulaqqu kuffaxa mulisa.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.AX / w / &gt;l;A / &gt;;fx / ULs.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/quxi.html#highlulani">Quxi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ru.html#highlulani">ru</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/ku.html#highlulani">ku</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/laqqu.html#highlulani">laqqu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kuffa.html#highlulani">kuffa</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/x/xa.html#highlulani">xa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mulisa.html#highlulani">mulisa</a>.
[e]<em>mountain</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>prs;gno</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">present gnomic</span></span> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>dat</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">dative</span></span><em>-money</em> give-<small-caps>dtv</small-caps> <em>fool</em>
[e]&ldquo;It is to the mountain that fools give money.&rdquo;[/d]
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Quxi ru (kalumulisa) kuffiluxa laqqu.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.AX / w / kWULs / &gt;;FWx / l;A.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/quxi.html#highlulani">Quxi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ru.html#highlulani">ru</a> (<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kalu.html#highlulani">kalu</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mulisa.html#highlulani">mulisa</a>) <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kuffa.html#highlulani">kuffa</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/-ilu.html#highlulani">-ilu</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/x/-xa.html#highlulani">-xa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/laqqu.html#highlulani">laqqu</a>.
[e]<em>mountain</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>prs;gno</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">present gnomic</span></span> (<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>abl</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">ablative</span></span>-<em>fool</em>) <em>give</em>-<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>psv</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">passive</span></span>-<small-caps>dtv</small-caps> <em>money</em>.
[e]&ldquo;It is to the mountain that money is given (by fools).&rdquo;[/d]
[2]Adposition
To promote a adpositional phrase to subject, prefix the verb with the adposition. The old subject is demoted to object. The old object, if any, is demoted to dative.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Mihu pi nijagaru gupi.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.MV / P / Njgw / &lt;P.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mihu.html#highlulani">Mihu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pi.html#highlulani">pi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/ni.html#highlulani">ni</a>-<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/jagaru.html#highlulani">jagaru</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/g/gupi.html#highlulani">gupi</a>.
[e]<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>3ani;int</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">animate third person intransitive</span></span> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>pst;sta</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">past stative</span></span> <em>at-sand</em> <em>sit</em>
[e]&ldquo;She sat in the sand.&rdquo;[/d]
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Jagaru pi nigupu quhu.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.jgw / P / N&lt;o / AV.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/jagaru.html#highlulani">Jagaru</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pi.html#highlulani">pi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/ni.html#highlulani">ni</a>-<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/g/gupi.html#highlulani">gupi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/quhu.html#highlulani">quhu</a>.
[e]<em>sand </em><span class="tooltip"><small-caps>pst;sta</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">past stative</span></span> <em>at</em>-<em>sit</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>3ani;tra</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">animate third person transitive</span></span>
[e]&ldquo;It was the sand that she sat in.&rdquo;[/d]
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Mihu pi nijagaru dasi nukki.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.MV / P / Njgw / dS / I;K.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mihu.html#highlulani">Mihu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pi.html#highlulani">pi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/ni.html#highlulani">ni</a>-<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/jagaru.html#highlulani">jagaru</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dasi.html#highlulani">dasi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/nukki.html#highlulani">nukki</a>.
[e]<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>3ani;int</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">animate third person intransitive</span></span> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>pst;sta</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">past stative</span></span><em> at-sand</em> <em>eat</em> <em>strawberry</em>
[e]&ldquo;He was eating a strawberry in the sand.&rdquo;[/d]
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Jagaru pi kunukki nidasi quhu.</strong>

[1]Dependent Clauses
A dependent clause is a clause that is unable to stand meaningfully by itself.
They are marked by having the auxiliary at the end.
[2]Subordinate Clauses
A subordinate clause is one introduced by a subordinating conjunction in the matrix clause. A comma is used to separate a subordinate from its matrix. The conjunction is placed on the side of the main clause that is closest to the subordinate. The clauses can be put in either order.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>&#x294;usu ru lu&rsquo;i fu daru&rsquo;i, <highlight>ba pu&rsquo;iba miku ra&rsquo;u</highlight>.</strong>

Here the subordinate clauses are hightlighted. The cause is subordinate to the effect.
[3]Location Adverbial Clauses
The word <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/ma.html#highlulani">ma</a> <high-lulani>m</high-lulani> <em>where</em> is often used as a prefix for adpositions used as clausal conjunctions.

[e]&ldquo;I loved you before your ball turned red.&rdquo;[/d]
[2]Content Clauses
A content clause is one that takes the place of a noun. They begin with the complementiser <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/li.html#highlulani">li</a> <high-lulani>L</high-lulani> and are separated from the matrix clause by commas. The auxiliary is not optional, and is given a low tone. Quote marks are used around reported speech, replacing the complementiser.

[2]Relative Clauses
Relative clauses specify the noun by describing it. They begin with the relativiser <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/x/xiku.html#highlulani">xiku</a> <high-lulani>X&gt;</high-lulani> and are placed before the modified noun, The auxiliary is not optional, and is given a rising tone. Only subjects can be relativised. Other cases must be promoted to subject.

[3]Intransitives
If the only argument of the relative verb is the modified noun, the auxiliary is appended to the verb, and the relativiser is dropped. This auxiliary is given a mid-tone.

[3]Transitives

[2]Questions and Requests
Questions and requests are main clauses, but have the same auxiliary movement as dependent clauses, and thus are treated alongside them here.
[3]Interrogatives
An interrogative is a question sentence. There are two main types, polar questions and content questions.
Polar questions are one in which the answer is &ldquo;yes&rdquo; or &ldquo;no&rdquo;. They are spoken with a rising tone on the last word. The auxiliaries are used to answer.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Lulani lu&rsquo;i suma ra&rsquo;u?</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.WlN / Wi / zm / ru.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lulani.html#highlulani">Lulani</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lu'i.html#highlulani">lu&rsquo;i</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/suma.html#highlulani">suma</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra'u.html#highlulani">ra&rsquo;u</a>?
[e]<em>queen love</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>1tra</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">first person transitive</span></span> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>prs;sta</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">present stative</span></span>?
[e]&ldquo;Does the queen love me?&rdquo;[/d]
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Ra&rsquo;u. / Ji. / Ruku. / Pi.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.P.w&gt;.J.ru.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra'u.html#highlulani">Ra&rsquo;u</a>. / <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/ji.html#highlulani">Ji</a>. / <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ruku.html#highlulani">Ruku</a>. / <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pi.html#highlulani">Pi</a>.
[e]<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>prs;sta</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">present stative</span></span>. / <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>prs;neg</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">present negative</span></span>. /  <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>fut;gno</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">future gnomic</span></span>. /  <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>pst;sta</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">past stative</span></span>.
[e]&ldquo;Yes.&rdquo; / &ldquo;No.&rdquo; / &ldquo;She will.&rdquo; / &ldquo;She did.&rdquo;[/d]
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Lulani nimalu ji?</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.WlN / NmW / J.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lulani.html#highlulani">Lulani</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/nimalu.html#highlulani">nimalu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/ji.html#highlulani">ji</a>?
[e]<em>queen bear</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>prs;neg</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">present negative</span></span>?
[e]&ldquo;Is the queen not a bear?&rdquo;[/d]
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Ji. / Ra&rsquo;u. / Na.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>n.ru.J</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/ji.html#highlulani">Ji</a>. / <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra'u.html#highlulani">Ra&rsquo;u</a>. / <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/na.html#highlulani">Na</a>.
[e]<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>prs;neg</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">present negative</span></span>. / <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>prs;sta</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">present stative</span></span>. / <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>prs;hab</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">present habitual</span></span>.
[e]&ldquo;Yes, she&rsquo;s not.&rdquo; / &ldquo;No, she is.&rdquo; / &ldquo;Usually.&rdquo;[/d]
If the focus of the question is on a particular noun, that noun receives a falling tone.
Content questions are ones in which the expected answer is more than just &ldquo;yes&rdquo; or &ldquo;no&rdquo;. These questions have a rising tone on the main question word itself.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Lulani lu&rsquo;i sama ra&rsquo;u?</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.WlN / Wi / sm / ru.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lulani.html#highlulani">Lulani</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lu'i.html#highlulani">lu&rsquo;i</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sama.html#highlulani">sama</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra'u%3F.html#highlulani">ra&rsquo;u?</a>
[e]<em>Queen love what</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>prs;sta</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">present stative</span></span>?
[e]&ldquo;Whom does the queen love?&rdquo;[/d]
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Kimilli. / Fu. / Cu&rsquo;i.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.yi.v.KM;L.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kimilli.html#highlulani">Kimilli</a>. / <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/fu.html#highlulani">Fu</a>. / <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/c/cu'i.html#highlulani">Cu&rsquo;i</a>.
[e]<em>King</em>. / <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>2tra</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">second person transitive</span></span>. / <em>Nothing</em>.
[e]&ldquo;The king.&rdquo; / &ldquo;You.&rdquo; / &ldquo;No one.&rdquo;[/d]
[3]Imperatives
An imperative statement is an order.
Second person imperatives are directed to the listener. In these, the subject is dropped, a future auxiliary in the appropriate aspect is suffixed to the verb, and this verb complex is moved to the end of the sentence. These are spoken with a falling tone on the auxiliary.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Lulani lu&rsquo;iruku!</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.WlN / Wiw&gt;.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lulani.html#highlulani">Lulani</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lu'i.html#highlulani">lu&rsquo;i</a>-<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ruku.html#highlulani">ruku</a>!
[e]<em>Queen love-</em><span class="tooltip"><small-caps>fut;gno</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">future gnomic</span></span>!
[e]&ldquo;Love the queen!&rdquo;[/d]&date=20180505--------------------------------------------------3
[1]Noun Phrases
The full noun phrase is made up of these components in the following order:
[n]adposition-
case marker-
number
relative clause
<highlight>main noun</highlight>
-determiner
-conjunction
-genitive marker
[/n]
The highlighted component denotes the only one that is compulsory, <em>i.e.</em>: the main noun itself. The hyphens represent the lack of a word space in both the Tinellbian script and the transcription.

[1]Gerunds
The gerund suffix <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/-ru.html#highlulani">-ru</a> <high-lulani>w</high-lulani> changes basic verbs into nouns describing the activity.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/h/huba.html#highlulani">huba</a>ru <high-lulani>Vbw</high-lulani> <em>breathing</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mala.html#highlulani">mala</a>ru <high-lulani>mlw</high-lulani><em> reflecting</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/miku.html#highlulani">miku</a>ru <high-lulani>M&gt;w</high-lulani> <em>being red</em>[/d]
Compound verbs, as well as those involving noun incorporation, can also be changed like this.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dissu'ahati.html#highlulani">dissu&rsquo;ahati</a>ru <high-lulani>D;zahTw</high-lulani> <em>feeling happy</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pakicu.html#highlulani">pakicu</a>ru<strong> </strong><high-lulani>pKyw</high-lulani> <em>believing to be true</em>

The genitive determiners, including <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/-qa.html#highlulani">-qa</a> <high-lulani>q</high-lulani>, allow for (only) the subject of the verb to be mentioned.

[1]Apocrypha
This section details particular categories of vocabulary items.
&date=20170716
--------------------------------------------------3
[1]Numbers
[2]Cardinal Numbers
High Lulani numbers are written with the positive digits (1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6 and 7), their negative counterparts (<overline>1</overline>, <overline>2</overline>, <overline>3</overline>, <overline>4</overline>, <overline>5</overline>, <overline>6</overline> and <overline>7</overline>) and a zero (0).
When writing out a number, each digit is worth fifteen times as much as the following digit. A period (fractional point: . ) is used to separate the integer part of the number from the mantissa. A comma (,) is used in the integer part to separate the digits into groupings of four, beginning from the fractional point.
[f]2 <em>two</em>
[e]5.<overline>3</overline> <em>four and four-fifths = five + (minus three &times; (fifteen ^ minus one</em></em>
[e]1<overline>7</overline> <em>eight = (one &times; fifteen) + (minus seven)</em>
[e]20 <em>thirty = (two &times; fifteen)</em>
[e]3<overline>2</overline>6 <em>six hundred and forty-one =
(three &times; (fifteen ^ two</em> + (minus two &times; fifteen) + six</em>
[e]<overline>1</overline>,34<overline>5</overline>3 <em>minus thirty-nine thousand, six hundred and seventy-two =
(minus one &times; (fifteen ^ four</em> + (three &times; (fifteen ^ three</em> +
(four &times; (fifteen ^ two</em> + (minus five &times; fifteen) + three</em>
[3]One-digit Numbers
